## Introduction: The Snarled Skein 

11

## Introduct 

Although the Weaver has certainly risen to the posi—_ powerful and subtle being, her influence not always evident tion of most powerful among the Triat, the Garou are oftwo —_and werewolves often overlook her doings in their pursuit of minds about her. Her function, like that of all the Triatic all things Wyrm-tainted. In fact, the line between the spirits, is of course necessary. Without her, physical beings © Weaver and the Wyrm is often fuzzy, so that Garou often and things would have no coherent form or function. There — mistake the Weaver’s works for those of the Wyrm, and would be no laws of nature to ensure that the worldranin _ react accordingly. Other times, the influence of the Wyrm an orderly fashion. Without the Weaver, all wouldbe chaos, _ is indeed more powerful and obvious, and the Weaver's role unformed, shifting matter and raw energy in a world where in the situation is ignored as incidental and irrelevant. In cause need not follow effect and no sentient being could —_ most cases nothing could be further from the truth. survive — if only because it would immediately go mad. In many ways, the Weaver still serves as an ally to many On the other hand, it isevident thatshe hasgonemuch — Garou, and certainly to humanity. However, in the grand too far. Her madness spurs her to attempt to calcify everyscheme of things, her mad spinnings are far from what the thing, both in the Umbra and on the physical plane, into _universe needs. Ifshe ever manages to throw off her madness static changelessness and dreary homogeneity. ManyGarou _and restrain herself, then there might be a chance for agree that she is quite mad, but do not realize just how so; nor balance once again. If not, then the ultimate result will be do they fully ken that this is her greatest weakness. She isa _a universe of pure and perfect order — of the lifeless sort.
